Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. Lily liked to pretend she was a popular princess. She lived in a big castle with her best friends, a cat and a dog.

One day, while playing in the castle, Lily found a big cobweb. The cobweb was in the way of her fun game. She wanted to get rid of it, but she was scared of the spider that lived there.

Lily asked her friends, the cat and the dog, to help her. They all worked together to clean the cobweb. The spider was sad, but it found a new home outside. Lily, the cat, and the dog were happy they could play without the cobweb in the way. And they all lived happily ever after.

Once upon a time, in a peaceful town, there lived a little boy named Tim. Tim loved to run and play outside. One day, Tim saw a race in the park. He was excited and wanted to join the race.

Tim went to his friend, Sarah, and said, "Let's start the race!" Sarah smiled and said, "Yes, let's go!" They lined up with the other kids and waited for the race to begin. When they heard the word "Go!", they started running as fast as they could.

Tim and Sarah ran with all their speed, laughing and having fun. They could feel the wind in their hair as they raced to the finish line. In the end, Tim won the race and Sarah came in second. They were both so happy and proud of themselves. They celebrated with their friends and had a great day at the park.

One day, a girl named Mia went for a walk. She saw a big, scary house. It had a tall door and small windows. Mia was brave, so she went inside the house.

In the house, Mia saw a birdcage. Inside the birdcage, there was a little bird. The bird was sad. It wanted to fly and be free. Mia wanted to help the bird.

Mia opened the birdcage door. The bird flew out and was happy. It was not scary anymore. Mia and the bird were friends. They played and had fun all day.

Once there were two friends named Bob and Sam. They were playing together in the garden one day. Sam picked a flower and then pointed to a black bird in a tree. 
"What's that?" he asked Bob.    

Bob smiled and said, "That's a Crow. Listen, what sound does it make?"

Suddenly, the crow made a loud sound that sounded like "Caw, Caw!"

"That's a Caw," Bob smiled.

Sam laughed and said, "I think I should pick a better word next time!"

Bob smiled and nodded. "That's a good idea. We should always pick the right word to use when we talk to each other."

The moral of the story is that it is important to choose the right words when you talk to your friends. Being thoughtful and using kind words can help keep friendships strong.

Jim was very frightened when he arrived at the barber's shop. It was his first time getting a haircut! He didn't want his mum to leave him alone with the strange man.

"Don't worry," said the barber. He smiled and handed Jim a big lollipop. "I'll look after you and give you the best haircut ever."

Jim's frown disappeared and he couldn't help but be excited. The barber put a cape around him, and the chair felt like a magic carpet ride. Soon, Jim felt his hair being trimmed, and the barber even gave him some funny glasses to look through. When Jim looked in the mirror, he saw the best haircut ever! He was so happy, he forgot all about being scared.

Mum smiled when she saw Jim. She was so proud of him for sitting so still for such a long time.

"Well done, my boy!" she said, giving him a big hug. 

Jim smiled and couldn't wait to show his friends his new haircut.

Once upon a time, there lived a little girl called Lucy. One day, Lucy was feeling very sad. She wanted to fly away so she could be happy but she was too young. 

Then, a bright flame appeared in the sky. She was scared at first, but then she saw that the flame was made of magic. 

Lucy asked the flame, "Can you let me fly away so I can be happy again?"

The flame answered, "Yes, I can permit you to fly away but first you must promise to take care of your family." 

Lucy smiled and said, "I will certainly take care of them. Please let me fly away!" 

The flame permitted Lucy to spread her arms and fly away into the night. She felt happy, free and no longer sad. Lucy waved goodbye to the flame and continued with her adventures.

Then, an old man showed up. He was very helpful and offered to help find a way to make the record work. He tried to figure out how to make the record work, but no matter how hard he tried, he couldn't make the record work. 

The 3 year old was very sad. He asked the old man, "Can you make it work?" 

The old man shook his head and said, "I'm sorry, but I can't make it work. I tried everything I could. I'm afraid the record will never work again." 

The 3 year old was very sad and never forgot the black record. The 3 year old never saw the old man again.

Once there was an old man. He saw an old brick and thought it would be fun to take it home to play with. So he went to steal it. 

He was hiding behind a tree when he heard someone coming. He saw it was a little girl. She looked at the old brick and said, "That'll be nice to have for building my house."

The old man said, "You can't take that. I'm going to steal it for myself."

The little girl replied, "Well, you can't do that. That's not nice."

The old man thought for a minute. Then he said, "How about I share it with you? We can both have it and play together."

The little girl smiled and said, "Yes, that sounds fun!"

The curtains were hanging cleanly in the windows of the little room. Every day, the girl would run in and whisper secrets to them. She hadn't noticed it before, but today, when she was talking in her very quietest voice, the curtains rustled as if in response. Her eyes grew wider as she heard what sounded like an echo of her own whisper. 

Curious, she asked the curtains, "Can you understand me?". The curtains didn't move. She whispered the question again and waited. She heard a faint whispering in response, but it wasn't the same as if she were speaking. This whisper felt different somehow. 

The girl waited and listened. Suddenly, the curtains moved again. This time they were pushing back, inviting her closer. As the girl looked closer, she saw a crack in the window and she could now hear more clearly the voice she had heard earlier. "Come here," it said. 

The girl took a deep breath, trembling with anticipation and excitement. She stepped closer and the curtain parted. Behind it was a secret garden. Everything was clean and vibrant and the girl felt more alive than she had ever felt before. She was finally on an adventure of her own. 

The girl and the whisper from the curtains had a lot more to share.

Mommy and Jimmy were walking down a path one night. It was dark, and their shadows were long. 
Jimmy said, "Mommy, look at my shadow. I want to let it run faster than any other shadow". 
"Oh no, Jimmy," Mommy said, "It's too dark outside. Let's just take a look at the shadows for now".
Jimmy said, "Okay, Mommy. Let's see how our shadows look like."
Mommy and Jimmy watched their shadows stretch across the path. They were long and thin like two dark lines in the night. 
Jimmy said, "Mommy, look, I can make my shadow go on a walk. It's so fun!"
Mommy smiled at Jimmy and said, "Let your shadow go on a walk. I'm sure it will have so much fun!" 
Jimmy smiled and with a little skip and a jump, his shadow went on its way. What fun they had that night!

Mia and Leo are friends. They like to play with toys and eat snacks. One day, Mia has a peanut. She likes peanuts. They are crunchy and salty. Leo does not have a peanut. He wants a peanut. He is jealous of Mia.

"Can I have your peanut?" Leo asks Mia.

"No, it is mine. You have a cracker. Eat your cracker," Mia says.

"But I want a peanut. Please, Mia, give me your peanut," Leo begs.

"No, no, no. Go away, Leo. Leave me alone," Mia says. She puts the peanut in her mouth and chews.

Leo is sad and angry. He does not like Mia. He does not want to be her friend. He thinks Mia is mean and selfish. He runs away from Mia and cries.

Mia hears Leo cry. She feels sorry for Leo. She does not want to make him cry. She does not want to lose her friend. She spits out the peanut and runs after Leo.

"Leo, Leo, wait. I am sorry. I was mean. You can have my peanut. Here, take it," Mia says. She gives Leo the peanut.

Leo stops crying. He looks at Mia and the peanut. He smiles. He takes the peanut and says, "Thank you, Mia. You are a good friend. I am sorry, too. I was jealous. Can we share the peanut?"

Mia nods. She smiles, too. She says, "Yes, we can share the peanut. And we can share the cracker, too. And we can play with toys and eat snacks. We are friends, Leo."

Leo and Mia hug. They share the peanut and the cracker. They play with toys and eat snacks. They are happy. They are friends.

"Lily, I don't want to cook. I want to play with my cars. You are too bossy. You do everything yourself." Tom says.

Lily is angry. She wants to cook with Tom. She thinks cooking is fun. She does not want to play with cars. She thinks cars are boring.

"Tom, you are silly. Cooking is fun. Cars are boring. You have to help me. We are a team. Mom will be happy if we cook a cake for her." Lily says.

Tom and Lily start to argue. They raise their voices. They make a mess. They spill the eggs, the flour, the milk, and the sugar. They drop the bowl, the spoon, and the pan. They do not notice mom coming home.

Mom sees the kitchen. She sees Lily and Tom. She is not happy. She is angry.

"Lily and Tom, what are you doing? Why are you making such a noise? Why are you making such a mess? You are not cooking. You are fighting. You are not a team. You are naughty." Mom says.

Lily and Tom feel sorry. They stop arguing. They apologize to mom. They help mom clean the kitchen. They hug mom. They say they love her.

Mom forgives Lily and Tom. She hugs them back. She says she loves them too. She says they can cook a cake together another day. She says they have to be nice to each other. She says they have to share and take turns. She says they have to have fun.

Lily and Ben were excited to go to the lake with their dad. They liked to swim, splash and play with the fish. They also liked to find logs and sticks to make boats and rafts.

"Look, dad, I found a big log!" Ben shouted, dragging a long piece of wood to the shore. "Can we make a boat with it?"

"Sure, Ben, that's a great log for a boat. Let's see if we can find some rope and a sail," dad said, smiling.

Lily ran to help Ben with the log. She saw a blue towel and a stick nearby. "I have an idea, Ben. We can use this towel as a sail and this stick as a mast. Then we can tie them to the log with this rope," she said, holding up the items.

"Wow, Lily, you are very smart. That's a good idea. Let's do it," Ben said, nodding.

They worked together to make the boat. They tied the rope around the log and the stick. They attached the towel to the stick with some knots. They made sure the boat was strong and stable.

"Are you ready, Ben?" Lily asked, holding the boat.

"Yes, I'm ready, Lily. Let's send our boat to the water," Ben said, grabbing the other end of the boat.

They lifted the boat and carried it to the edge of the lake. They counted to three and pushed the boat into the water. The boat floated and the wind blew the sail.

"Look, dad, look! Our boat is sailing!" Lily and Ben shouted, jumping and clapping.

"Wow, you two, you made a wonderful boat. I'm very proud of you. Let's watch it go," dad said, hugging them.

One day, Sara and Ben see a big truck outside their house. It has many cans of paint and brushes. A man gets out of the truck. He is a painter. He comes to their door and talks to Mommy. He says he will paint their house a new color. Mommy says yes and shows him the house.

Sara and Ben are curious. They want to see the painter work. They follow him to the back of the house. He opens a can of paint. It is blue. He dips his brush in the paint and starts to paint the wall. Sara and Ben think it looks pretty. They want to help.

They find some crayons and papers. They draw pictures of the painter and the house. They use blue, yellow, and red. They make the pictures wild and fun. They show them to the painter. He smiles and says they are very good. He says they are artists.

Sara and Ben are happy. They thank the painter for his nice words. They give him their pictures as a gift. He thanks them and says he will keep them. He says they are his friends. Sara and Ben hug him and say they are his friends too. They go back to Mommy and tell her about the painter. Mommy says they are very sweet and polite. She says she is proud of them. Sara and Ben smile and hug Mommy. They like the painter and the new color of their house.

Once upon a time, there was a little bunny named Benny. Benny was very poor and had no food to eat. One day, Benny decided to go on a journey to find some food. He hopped through the forest and over the hills.

After a while, Benny met a kind deer. The deer asked Benny where he was going. Benny told the deer that he was on a journey to find some food because he was very hungry. The deer whispered to Benny that he knew where there was a big carrot patch. Benny was so happy and thanked the deer.

Benny finally found the carrot patch, but just as he was about to take a bite, a big, mean fox appeared. The fox wanted to eat Benny for dinner! Benny tried to run away, but he was too slow. The fox caught him and had him for dinner. Poor Benny!

Once upon a time, there was a little girl named Lily. She loved to play outside and explore the world around her. One day, she went to her grandma's house for lunch. Her grandma made her favorite food - spaghetti with a spicy sauce.

Lily loved the taste of the spicy sauce, but she didn't realize that it would make her mouth feel hot. She ate and ate, not realizing that she was getting hotter and hotter. Suddenly, she felt like she needed something to cool her down.

That's when she saw it - a big glass of cold milk on the table. She reached out to grab it, but her hand slipped and she accidentally knocked over a whip that was on the table. The whip fell to the ground with a loud thud.

Lily's grandma quickly got up to grab the whip and put it away. Lily was relieved that she didn't get in trouble, but she knew she had to be more careful in the future. From that day on, she always made sure to grab things carefully and pay attention to her surroundings.

She went home and told her friends about the bird that struck the ground. They were all surprised and wished they could see the bird too.

When they arrived at the beach, Tim wanted to go swimming. His mom told him to wait a minute while she put sunscreen on him. Tim didn't like the sunscreen because it felt tight on his skin. "Mom, I don't want to wear this! It's too tight!" he said.

His mom explained that the sunscreen was important to protect his skin from the sun, which can be harmful. "Just like how we need oxygen to breathe, our skin needs protection from the sun," she said. Tim understood and agreed to wear the sunscreen. They had a great day at the beach and Tim was happy he listened to his mom's advice.

Once upon a time, there was a little orange cat named Mimi. Mimi had a long tail that she loved to play with. One day, Mimi was walking in the park when she saw a little girl.

"Hello, little girl," said Mimi.

"Hi, kitty," said the little girl. "Your tail is so long!"

"Yes, it is," said Mimi. "Do you understand why cats have long tails?"

"No, why?" asked the little girl.

"Well," said Mimi, "we use our tails to help us balance when we climb and jump."

"Oh, I see," said the little girl. "Can I pet your tail?"

"Of course!" said Mimi, and the little girl gently petted her soft orange tail.

Lila and Lulu were twins. They liked to play with their dolls. They had many dolls, but their favorite was Molly. Molly had smooth hair and a pretty dress.

One day, Lila and Lulu had a fight. Lila wanted to play with Molly, but Lulu said no. She said Molly was her doll. Lila said no, Molly was their doll. They both pulled Molly's arms. Molly's dress ripped.

Lila and Lulu stopped pulling. They looked at Molly. They felt sad. They had hurt their doll. They had hurt each other.

"I'm sorry, Lulu," Lila said. "I didn't mean to rip Molly's dress."

"I'm sorry, Lila," Lulu said. "I didn't mean to be mean to you."

They hugged each other. They hugged Molly. They said they loved each other. They loved Molly.

They went to their mom. They showed her Molly's dress. They told her what happened. Mom smiled. She said she was proud of them for saying sorry. She said she could fix Molly's dress.

She took Molly and a needle and some thread. She sewed Molly's dress. She made it look new. She gave Molly back to Lila and Lulu. They thanked her. They said they would share Molly. They said they would not fight.

They went back to their room. They played with Molly. They made her shake her smooth hair. They made her talk. They made her laugh. They laughed too. They were happy. They were twins.

The pile of twigs is not just twigs. It is a nest for bees. The bees do not like Lily and Ben taking their twigs. They get angry and fly out of the nest. They buzz very loud and sting Lily and Ben all over.

Lily and Ben scream and cry. They drop the twigs and run to Mom. Mom hugs them and takes them to the car. She drives them to the doctor. The doctor gives them medicine and bandages. He says they will be okay, but they have to stay home for a few days.

Lily and Ben are very sad. They do not like bees. They do not like twigs. They do not want to visit the park again. They wish they had listened to Mom.

One day, he went to the park with his mom. He saw a big ice cream truck. He ran to it and asked for a cone. The man gave him a cone with three scoops: chocolate, vanilla and strawberry. Tommy was very happy. He thanked the man and paid with his mom's money.

He walked back to his mom, holding his cone carefully. He saw a little girl on a bench. She had no ice cream. She looked sad. Tommy felt sorry for her. He wanted to share his ice cream with her. He walked to her and said, "Hi, I'm Tommy. Do you want some of my ice cream? It's delicious."

The little girl smiled. She said, "Hi, I'm Lily. Thank you, that's very nice of you. I would love some of your ice cream." She took a lick of the strawberry scoop. She said, "Mmm, this is my favorite flavor. You are very kind, Tommy."

Tommy and Lily became friends. They shared the cone and talked. They had fun. Tommy's mom saw them and smiled. She was proud of Tommy. She knew he had a big heart. She thought, "Sharing is caring. Tommy learned a good lesson today."

One day, they are playing with shapes and they have a problem. Anna wants to use the red triangle for her house roof, but Ben wants to use it for his rocket nose. They both reach for the red triangle at the same time and pull on it.

"Let go! It's mine!" Anna says.

"No, it's mine! I saw it first!" Ben says.

They talk loud and angry. They do not want to share the red triangle. They do not want to play with other shapes. They do not want to play with each other.

Mom hears them and comes to see what is wrong. She sees them fighting over the red triangle and the other shapes on the floor.

"What is going on here?" Mom asks.

"Anna took my red triangle!" Ben says.

Tim and Sam were friends who liked to draw with crayons. They had many colors of crayons, but they both loved orange the most. They always wanted to use the orange crayon for their pictures.

One day, they found only one orange crayon in their box. They both reached for it at the same time. They pulled and tugged, but neither of them would let go.

"Give me the orange crayon!" Tim said. "I saw it first!"

"No, I did!" Sam said. "It's mine!"

They started to yell and fight over the orange crayon. They did not seem like friends anymore.

Their teacher saw them and came over. She was not happy. She took the orange crayon from them and said, "You two need to learn to share. If you can't share, you can't play with the crayons at all."

She put the orange crayon away and gave them each a different color. Tim got a blue crayon and Sam got a green crayon. They looked at their crayons and felt sad. They missed the orange crayon.

They looked at each other and felt sorry. They realized they had been silly and mean. They decided to say sorry and make up.

"I'm sorry, Sam," Tim said. "You can have the orange crayon next time."

"I'm sorry, Tim," Sam said. "You can have it now. I like green too."

They hugged and smiled. They started to draw with their crayons. They made a picture of a sun with the orange crayon and a grass with the green crayon. They added a sky with the blue crayon. They wrote their names on the picture and gave it to their teacher.

Their teacher was proud of them. She said, "That's a beautiful picture. And you know what? You two are beautiful friends. You learned to share and be kind. That's more important than any color."

Tim and Sam nodded and agreed. They learned that sharing is caring. And that orange is not the only color.

Once upon a time, there was a very bossy caterpillar. He decided he wanted to take a walk. He hiked and hiked, looking far and wide. Then he stumbled upon a garden. Inside, he saw the most beautiful flowers! He was so amazed, he just had to take a closer look.

At the same moment, a butterfly flew by! She invited the caterpillar to come and explore with her. So he joined her and together, they went from flower to flower. Then the caterpillar found a patch of soft, sweet grass. He wanted to stay and yield, but the butterfly was ready to head back to the sky. 

The caterpillar said goodbye to his new friend and crawled into the warm grass. He curled up for a restful nap. Soon, he felt his body becoming longer and fuzzier. He opened his eyes and saw that he had become a beautiful butterfly! He flew high into the sky and thanked the butterfly who had helped him transform. 

The caterpillar was no longer bossy - he was free! He flew around the garden, never forgetting the lesson he had learned.

Once upon a time, there was a sleepy bunny named Ben. Ben lived in a big forest with many trees and vines. One day, Ben saw a tasty vine hanging from a tree. He wanted to eat it, but it was too high for him to reach.

Ben had a friend named Tim, a tall giraffe. He thought Tim could help him get the vine. He went to Tim and mentioned the vine he wanted to eat. Tim agreed to help Ben, but only if Ben would help him find some tasty leaves later.

Together, they went to the tree with the vine. Tim lifted Ben up, and Ben got the vine. After that, Ben helped Tim find the best leaves to eat. They both shared their food and were very happy.

The moral of the story is that when we help each other, we can solve our problems and make everyone happy.

Once upon a time, in a big sea, there was a sleepy fish named Bob. Bob lived near a reef with many other fish. One day, Bob woke up and saw that his friend, the starfish, was gone. He felt sad and decided to search for his friend.

Bob swam around the reef and asked his other friends, "Have you seen the starfish?" They all said no. But one fish told Bob, "I heard a big fish talking about a starfish. Maybe it's your friend!" Bob thanked the fish and continued his search.

Bob found the big fish and asked, "Have you seen my friend, the starfish?" The big fish smiled and said, "Yes, I found him stuck in the reef. I helped him get out, and he went home." Bob was happy and swam back to the reef. There, he found his friend, the starfish, safe and sound. They were both so happy to see each other and played together all day long.

Once upon a time, there was a little fish named Fin. Fin lived in the big sea with his family. They had a small home near some rocks. One day, Fin saw a big fish and wanted to become big like it.

Fin asked his mom, "Mom, how can I become big like that fish?" His mom said, "Fin, you will become big when you grow up. Just eat your food and play with your friends."

But Fin didn't want to wait. He swam far away from his home to find a way to become big. He saw a big, dark cave and went inside. In the cave, he found a magic rock that could make him big.

Fin touched the rock and said, "I want to become big now!" Suddenly, he became very big. He was happy, but he didn't know that the rock was bad. As he swam back home, he was so big that he broke his family's home by accident. His family was sad and had no place to live. Fin wished he had listened to his mom and waited to become big.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tim. He liked to play near the old creek. It was fun to throw rocks and watch the water splash.

One day, Tim saw a big, sharp stick near the creek. He wanted to play with it. But his mom said, "No, Tim! That stick is too sharp. It can hurt you."

Tim was sad, but he knew his mom was right. He left the sharp stick and went back to throwing rocks in the creek. And he had lots of fun playing safely by the water.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Tim. Tim was not feeling well, so his mom gave him a pill to help him feel better. Tim looked at the pill and thought it was too big for him. He did not want to take it.

Tim's friend, Sam, came to visit. Sam saw the pill and asked, "Why did you not take the pill, Tim?" Tim said, "It is too big, and I am scared." Sam was not selfish and wanted to help. "Let me pass it to you, and I will help you take it," Sam said.

With Sam's help, Tim took the pill. Soon, Tim felt much better. He was happy that Sam was not selfish and helped him. They played together all day and had lots of fun. Tim learned that it is good to have friends who help when you need it.

One day, a girl named Ann and her sister, Jane, went to the park. They saw a man playing a drum. They liked the sound and started to clap. The man smiled and played more.

Ann said, "I want to play too!" Jane was ignorant and did not know what a drum was. She asked, "What is that?" Ann told her, "It's a drum, silly!"

They took turns playing the drum and clapping. They had a fun day at the park with the drum man. At the end of the day, they went home and told their mom about the fun they had.

One day, a boy named Tim went to the store with his mom. He saw a green fruit called an avocado. Tim's tummy was hurt, so he asked his mom, "Can I eat this?"

His mom said, "I recommend you try it. It might help your hurt tummy feel better."

At home, Tim's sister, Sue, wanted the avocado too. They both wanted to eat it, but there was only one. Tim said, "My tummy hurts, so I should eat it." Sue said, "But I want it too!"

Mom came in and said, "I will buy more avocados tomorrow. You can share this one today." Tim and Sue shared the avocado, and Tim's hurt tummy felt better. They were happy to share and play together.

Once upon a time, there was a gentle bunny named Lucy. Lucy loved to skip and play with her friends in the sunny meadow. One day, Lucy and her friends decided to watch a movie together.

They found a movie about a big, happy family of animals. Lucy and her friends sat down and watched the movie. They laughed and clapped as the animals on the screen played and had fun together.

When the movie was over, Lucy and her friends went outside to play. They skipped and hopped, just like the animals in the movie. They were all very happy and had a great day together.

Once upon a time, there was a little boy called Joe. He was only 3 years old and he loved to stay outside and play with his friends. One day, Joe wanted to climb up to the top of a big tree in the backyard. His mom said it was okay, so he started climbing. 

When he reached the top, he was so happy! But then he saw something wild! A large bird was sitting in the tree and it didn't look very friendly. Joe was scared, but he decided to stay and see what would happen. 

The bird said to Joe: "You should not stay here! It is too dangerous!" But Joe was scared, he didn't know what to do. Then the bird flew away very quickly, and Joe was left alone on the top of the tree. 

It got dark outside, and Joe started to cry. He wanted to get down, but he was too scared to move. He stayed up there, feeling cold and hungry, until the morning came. 

Joe's mom found him the next morning, still on the top of the tree. She was so worried, and thankfully Joe was safe, but he never went climbing again.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl. She had hair as yellow as the sun, and a smile that shone brighter than all the stars in the sky. The little girl requested her mum to open the drawer in the kitchen. Her mum obliged, and the little girl let out an excited yelp of joy.

Inside the drawer, there were amazing things! Bars of chocolate, colourful plastic badges, and a toy car. The little girl was so excited that she couldn't pick just one thing. She took out all of the amazing items in the drawer and placed them on the kitchen table.

She smiled and thanked her mum as she raced out of the kitchen with her treasures. The little girl was so happy with the amazing items in the drawer that she told all of her friends in the playground about it. Everyone was so excited to come visit her and explore the drawer!

Lily wanted a pen. She kept asking her mom for one but her mom said she had to wait until she was old enough. So, Lily patiently waited for the day when she could own a pen. 

Finally, her mom said she was old enough and took her to the store to pick out her first pen. Inside the store, Lily saw so many pens. There were big ones, small ones, colorful ones, regular ones, etc. 

But, Lily decided to pick a regular pen. It was gray and just the right size to fit in her hand. She held her new pen in her hands and could not believe that it was her own. 

Lily happily ran out of the store with her new pen. She was so excited! She would practice writing with her regular pen everyday and soon she would be able to write just like her mom.

Once upon a time there was a little girl who loved to play. She wanted to join all the big kids in their favorite game. The game was to shoot arrows at a target and try to hit it.

The little girl wanted to join in, but she didn't have an arrow. Everyone else was very competitive and she was scared they would not let her play.

The little girl was sad until she saw a stick in the grass and picked it up. She brought it to the target and set it up.

The little girl took a deep breath and then reached into the grass to pick up three stones. She closed her eyes and threw the stones one by one.

The stones flew through the air and struck the stick. The little girl was so surprised when she opened her eyes, her arrow had hit the target!

The big kids cheered and the little girl was so happy she could take part in the game. From then on, the little girl learned to shoot arrows and was the most competitive of all.

Frankie was very excited. He had a new puppy and it needed a name. So, he thought and thought and thought. He couldn't decide and then he had a great idea! He decided to paint a picture of his pup and give it a name based on the painting. He got out his paints and chose blue, yellow, and green. He started to paint, and when he was finished he saw the most beautiful puppy. It had sparkling blue eyes, wiggly yellow ears and a soft green nose. Frankie had named his puppy - Unknown!

Alice was a 3 year old girl who lived in a small house with her mom. Every day she would put on her shoes and go with mom to the park.

Alice always had a lot of fun at the park. She would often find something different, like the soap bubbles her mom made with her hands.

"Look at the bubbles mom!" said Alice.

Her mom smiled. "It's amazing what soap can do! It can make all sorts of different things, like bubbles or a beautiful painting."

Alice looked around the park. She imagined what was possible with soap. "I think I can make a big castle," she said.

Her mom gave her a hug. "I'll support you. Let's go get some soap and have some fun."

Alice smiled. She was excited to see what she could create with soap. The day was full of surprises.

One day, the boy was busy playing with his toys. He was having so much fun that he didn't want to leave. Suddenly he found something very unusual on the floor beside him. It looked like a big yellow lemon. He quickly picked it up and wanted to know what it was. 

He asked his mom, and she told him it was a lemon. He asked why it was in his room, and she said it had been left behind by the grocery store delivery man. 

The boy thought it was fascinating, and started to play with the lemon. He held it in his hands, squeezed it, and smelled it carefully. After a while, he decided to make a lemonade. He asked his mom for help, and together they made the most delicious lemonade ever. 

After seeing him so busy, his mom decided it was time for him to take a break. She told him to leave the lemon and take a nap. The boy did as he was told, and went to take a nap. 

When he woke up, he was happy to find that the lemon was still there. He had a great time playing with it - and drinking the lemonade he and his mom made - and was happy he could leave the lemon there for their next adventure.

Once upon a time, there was a little tree. It was very young, but it liked to grow. So every day, it would try to get bigger.

One day, though, something bad happened. A mean, ignorant person chopped the little tree into a bunch of pieces. The little tree was so sad and angry!

But then something wonderful happened. The pieces of the little tree started to grow! Even though it was chopped into pieces, it was still able to grow.

Eventually, the pieces grew into a big and beautiful tree. The tree was even bigger than it used to be!

At the end, the little tree taught everyone an important lesson: you should never give up, no matter how ignorant someone is.

Once upon a time, there was a young boy named John. He was very gifted, and had lots of toys. One day, he spotted a big ship sailing near his house. He was so excited to get on board!

John asked his mom if he could go on the ship, but she said no. "It's too dangerous, sweetheart," she said. So, John made a plan to steal the ship and sail away.

He packed a bag of food and some clothes and sneaked onto the ship. As he was sailing away, John shouted, "I'm taking this ship on a journey!"

Suddenly, he saw the ship's captain, who yelled, "Oh no! You can't take this ship!" John was very scared and he started to cry.

The captain was very kind and said, "It's ok. I understand why you wanted to steal the ship. You can stay on board and help me sail this ship!"

John was really happy and agreed to stay. From then on, he and the captain started having many great adventures together!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Joe. He was three years old and he was always very happy.

One day, Joe wanted to go on a big adventure. He decided to take a trip to the tip. Joe was so excited, but he was a little worried too. He was scared that the trip might be a bit boring.

So Joe decided to ask his mum for help. His mum gave him a big bag full of fun toys and she showed him the best way to get to the tip.

Once there was a brave knight. He was traveling in a far away land when he saw a volcano. He was very curious, so he decided to explore it. He rode closer, and the ground began to shake. He looked around and saw thick smoke spewing out of the volcano. 

The brave knight was determined to explore it, so he got off his horse and began to climb. He was surprised to see that the volcano looked much bigger up close. He kept climbing, and finally reached the top. 

When he looked inside, his heart sank. He saw bubbling lava rising up and down. But before he could turn around and run, a giant dragon flew out of the volcano. 

The dragon glared at the brave knight. He could feel his courage weakening, but he still tried to fight it. He grabbed his sword, but the dragon just roared and nodded its head. The knight was filled with fear and he ran as fast as he could away from the volcano. He never looked back.

The little girl was so happy to get the new telephone that she made sure to keep it safe with her this time. She kept it by her side all the time just to make sure she wouldn't lose it again. From that day onwards, she was careful to always keep her telephone safe.

Sophie was very sad, but then she realized something. She had been dreaming about the laser! Suddenly she was happy again and she thanked the stars for letting her dream such wonderful things.

John was very organized. Every morning he would bring his carpet to school. On the carpet were many special toys. They were kept in a special way so they were easy to find. 
At recess, John would unroll the carpet. All the children would gather around. Everyone loved to play the games. John would organize a game of tag and the children would laugh and giggle as they ran around. 
John would also organize a hide and seek game. Everyone would hide behind the carpet. Then, when the seeker found them, they would all burst into laughter. 
At the end of the day, John would roll up the carpet and take it home, looking forward to the next day when he could bring back his favorite carpet again.

One day the sky was grey. It was starting to rain. It was so silly!

The rain started to pitter-patter on the ground. The trees were dripping with water. All the people outside ran for cover.

Nancy was watching from her bedroom window. She saw the funny sight of people running away from the rain. It made her giggle.

But she didn't mind the rain too much. She ran outside and twirled under the raindrops. It felt so cool and refreshing.

The rain eventually stopped and the sun came out. Everything was so sparkly and colourful. What a silly sight! Nancy smiled, happy to be outside again.

Once upon a time, there was a bright alert blue bird who lives on top of a tall tree. One clear day, the sun was shining so brightly that the bird could no longer stay awake. So, the bird paused for a moment and decided to take a nap in the sun.

Suddenly, the bird was awoken with a loud noise. It was the sound of thunder! The blue bird spread its wings wide and flew to an empty branch just as the sky was getting grey. Cautiously, the bird looked around and saw a storm building up in the sky.

The bird then paused again, as if it was building up the courage to fly to safety. With one flutter of its wings, the bird set off, faster and faster, trying to catch up with the dark clouds. The storm was getting bigger and bigger and it was getting windier and windier. 

Finally, the bird managed to stay ahead of the storm and landed safely on a tree in a sunny spot on the other side. The blue bird was happy that it had made it in time, and it watched the storm fly away with its bright alert eyes.

Once, there was a little girl named Lisa. She was only three years old. One day, it started raining very hard outside of her window. Lisa looked out the window and saw her trees and the street shivering in the wind. 

Lisa's mom came into her bedroom and said, "Lisa, we need to take a shower so that you don't get cold." Lisa's eyes lit up and she shouted, "Yay! A shower!" She was excited to play in the water. 

Her mom took her into the bathroom and helped her undress. Lisa stepped into the shower and the warm water made her shiver with delight. She started splashing around, playing with the water and the foam. 

After the shower, Lisa dried herself and put on some warm clothes. She ran to her bedroom and said to her mom, "Let's go outside and play!" Her mom smiled and told her, "We can go outside after I finish cooking dinner. It will be slow, so you must be patient."

Once upon a time, there was a little goat named Sammy. Sammy was a very happy goat who loved to play in the fields all day long. But one day, Sammy was feeling worried. He didn't know why, but he just felt something wasn't right.

So Sammy went to his friend, the farmer, and asked him, "What's wrong? Why do I feel so worried?" The farmer just shrugged and said, "I don't know, Sammy. Maybe something bad is going to happen. Let's keep a look out."

So Sammy kept an eye out all day, looking for anything suspicious. He saw some birds flying and some animals scurrying around, but nothing out of the ordinary.

Finally, the farmer came out and said, "Well, Sammy, I think everything is okay. Let's go out and have some fun."

So they played in the fields all day, and Sammy forgot all about his worries. He had a great time, and knew that all was right in the world.

Mary and her brother Sam love to play together. One day they decided to clap their hands and see who could clap the loudest. Sam clapped extra loudly, and Mary clapped extra fast. 

Mama heard the noise and came in to see what was going on. She saw Mary and Sam clapping, and she smiled.

Mama said, "You two were being very naughty, but because you were having fun I will give you each a cookie!"

With that, Mary and Sam stopped clapping and each one grabbed a cookie. They were both very happy. 

Mama said that from now on, they had to be good whenever they clapped because it was too loud. Mary and Sam agreed, giggling and eating their cookies. 

The two had so much fun together, and Mama was happy to see them happy.

Once upon a time, there was a rabbit who liked to go on adventures. She liked to explore the world around her.

One day, the rabbit found a valley filled with different kinds of flowers. She was so excited that she started hopping around in glee.

The rabbit asked her friends, "Do you want to explore the valley with me?"

But her friends didn't want to go, so the rabbit decided to venture off alone.

As she hopped and explored the valley, she noticed something different. It seemed like something was calling her to come closer.

Suddenly, she saw a tall figure at the end of the valley. She approached the figure and it was then that realized it was a giant. 

The giant smiled warmly at the rabbit and said, "I've been waiting for you, little one. Let's rest in the valley together."

The rabbit smiled and knew that the valley was her special place. She and the giant stayed there often, talking and resting together under the stars. The rabbit's adventures were always different-- filled with joy and laughter.

Once upon a time, there was a farmer and his sheep. The farmer lived on a big farm full of dirt and mud. 
One day, the farmer was looking for his sheep but he could not find them. He looked everywhere for them but he could not see them. He was worried and started to yell.

Suddenly, he heard a loud "baa!" He looked through the mud and saw the sheep! But they were dirty! He had to get them out of the mud.

The farmer yelled at the sheep to try and get them out of the mud. The sheep started jumping and jumping. Finally, the farmer got them out safely. 

The farmer was relieved and he gave the sheep a big hug. He was so happy that the sheep were safe and not hurt. From that day on, the farmer was extra careful when watching his sheep.

One day, a kid went to the beach. He was excited to explore the deep blue ocean. He blinked and looked around. Suddenly, he heard a voice that said: "Look out, it's too deep!"

The kid remembered what the voice said. He decided to be careful and not to go too far in the water. He kept blinking and looking around. He saw other kids playing and having fun in the shallow water.

The kid was happy that he listened to the voice and stayed in shallow water. He realized that sometimes it can be easy to get in trouble if you don't listen to warnings. He sang happily and had lots of fun with his friends.

This experience taught the kid to be careful and always listen to warnings. He knew it was important to listen to those who care. So, whenever he went to the beach, he never went too far into the water and always looked out for danger.

Once upon a time there was a little girl named Daisy. She liked to do yoga. One day, her mom suggested that she take a serious yoga class. So Daisy found a seat in the classroom and listened to the teacher.

The teacher said, "Tonight, we will start with a very serious yoga pose. It's very tricky and it takes lots of practice." Daisy thought it sounded fun, so she eagerly nodded her head.

But then, Daisy started to think: what if she couldn't do this tricky yoga pose? Would she still be able to do yoga? Daisy was getting more and more worried, so she asked her teacher what would happen. 

The teacher replied, "If you don't get this pose right, then you can't do yoga anymore." Daisy was sad and scared, but she tried her best. Unfortunately, Daisy couldn't do the pose and her teacher said she would have to leave the class.

And they all lived sadly ever after.

Once upon a time there was a very fragile bird. She lived in a lovely tree in the woods. Every day she went out and searched for tasty bugs.

But one day a big scary cat leapt out of the bushes and tried to grab her. She flew away as fast as she could and wasn't caught, but she dropped some of the bugs she was carrying. 

The fallen bugs became waste that was spread around the forest. The poor fragile bird was very sad that the yummy bugs were now waste.

So she worked hard to pick up all of the waste and put it back in the tree. Now every day the bird can eat all of the tasty bugs she can find, without having to worry about the big scary cat!

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Jacob. Jacob liked to go to the park and play. One day, he went to the park to look for his friends.

As he walked, he saw an orange bird perched on a branch of a tree. Jacob was amazed and he whispered, "What is that beautiful bird?".

The orange bird fluttered its wings and chirped. Jacob noticed that the bird seemed sad, so he said, "Would you like some help?".

The orange bird started to pray to God. Jacob joined in, and together they prayed for happiness. As they finished praying, the orange bird flew away.

Once upon a time, there was a little girl called Lily. Lily was only three years old and loved to explore the world. She didn't know what could be in the woods and often played around it.

One day, as she was walking, she heard something strange coming from a jar by her feet. When she opened it, a big, scary monster was inside. The monster was so terrible that she screamed.

The monster said, "Don't be scared, Lily. We just want to play with you."

Lily was so frightened she couldn't speak. She ran away from the jar and left the monster inside.

When she got home, she told her parents about the scary monster in the jar. They were so relieved that she was safe and warned her about how dangerous it is to play in the woods.

After that, Lily learned a valuable lesson about being careful and only going to places that she feels safe in. Although some things can be scary, if you stay brave, everything will be okay.

Once upon a time there was a small sunflower called Willow. Willow was so small every day she had to balance precariously on her thin stem. To make matters worse, the wind was always blowing and Willow had to work hard to stay standing.

But Willow was persistent. She held her head high, even when the wind increased in strength. Then one day something amazing happened. A group of children stopped at her field and the smallest gave her a lovely smile.

Willow couldn't believe it: she had made a friend at last.

But suddenly the wind blew even harder. Willow felt herself losing her balance. She desperately looked to her new friend for help but he had gone.

Willow felt helpless. The wind blew her over and she was never seen again. And the little sunflower never made any more friends.

Once upon a time, there was a happy boy named Jack. He lived in a little blue house with his mom and dad.

One day, Jack was running in the big backyard. The sun was shining and he felt so good. As he ran, he saw something sparkly in the grass. It was a bottle of perfume!

Jack picked it up and he sniffed it. It smelled so nice and he smiled. Then he ran to find his mom.

Jack found his mom in the kitchen and said, "Mom, look at what I found!" She smiled and said, "That's a very nice smell."

Just then, his brother Tommy walked into the kitchen. He saw the perfume and he got jealous. He yelled, "That's not fair! I want some too!" Jack just laughed and ran away with the perfume in his hand.

Once upon a time there was a little girl called Sally who loved to explore. One day, she discovered a special tree that she had never seen before. The tree was covered in bright yellow and orange fruit.

"Wow!" Sally said, staring in amazement. She reached up and grabbed one of the pieces of heavy fruit and held it in her hands. She decided to take it home and tell her mum all about it.

When they got home, Sally showed the fruit to her mum.

"What is it, sweetheart?" her mum asked.

"I don't know," Sally said.

Her mum cut the fruit open and smiled. "It's a mango," she said. "It's a very special fruit. You can eat it."

Sally tasted the mango and it was delicious. She smiled and thanked her mum.

Every day afterwards, Sally would go back to the special tree and tell her mum all about what she found.

Once upon a time there was a bear named Bobby. He was loyal to his family and always played sports with them. He was the best of all the animals at sport.

One day Bobby decided to rise up early in the morning and surprise his family with a game of sport. He went off to find a perfect spot for the game. But when he came to it, he found that the spot was too small for all the animals! Bobby was so disappointed.

Bobby thought and thought about what to do and he decided to build a bigger field. With lots of determination, he worked hard for many days, picking stones, collecting soil, and planting grass. Finally, the field was ready and he invited everyone to the big game.

All the animals gathered at the field and cheered for Bobby, the loyal bear. Bobby was so proud and the game was so much fun. From that day on, they all rose up early in the morning to play sports with Bobby!

Sara and Ben love to play in the garden. They like to dig, water, and plant seeds. They also like to look for bugs and birds. Sometimes they pretend to be animals or fairies.

One day, they find a big, shiny stone in the garden. It is round and smooth and has many colors. Sara picks it up and says, "Look, Ben, what a pretty stone! Maybe it is magic!"

Ben takes the stone and says, "Maybe it can make us become anything we want! Let's try it!"

They close their eyes and wish very hard. Sara wishes to become a butterfly, and Ben wishes to become a lion. They open their eyes and look at each other.

But nothing has changed. They are still Sara and Ben, holding the stone. They feel sad and confused.

"Maybe the stone is broken," Sara says.

"Or maybe we need to say a magic word," Ben says.

They try different words, like "abracadabra", "please", and "banana". But nothing works.

They are about to give up, when they hear a voice.

"Hello, children. What are you doing with my stone?"

They turn around and see a lady with a big hat and a basket. She is smiling and has a mild voice.

She is the gardener. She tells them that the stone is not magic, but a special kind of rock that she found in the mountains. She says that she likes to keep it in the garden, because it makes her happy.

She also tells them that they don't need a stone to become anything they want. They can use their imagination and their creativity. She says that she likes to pretend to be a bird or a flower sometimes.

She invites them to join her in the garden, and shows them how to make crowns and necklaces with leaves and flowers. She also teaches them the names of the plants and the animals.

Sara and Ben forget about the stone. They have fun with the gardener, and learn many new things. They decide that the garden is a magical place, after all.

Sara and Ben are playing in the yard. They like to run and jump and laugh. The sky is blue and the sun is bright. They are happy.

But then they hear a loud sound. Boom! Boom! Boom! It is a storm. The sky is dark and the wind is strong. They see flashes of light and hear more booms. They are scared.

They run to the house and knock on the door. "Mom! Mom! Let us in!" they cry. But no one answers. They knock again and again. But still no answer. Where is Mom?

They look around and see a red car in the driveway. It is Mom's car. They run to the car and open the door. They see Mom sitting in the front seat. She has a phone in her hand. She is talking to someone.

"Mom! Mom! There is a storm! We are scared!" they shout. Mom looks at them and smiles. She puts down the phone and hugs them.

"I'm sorry, my loves. I didn't hear you. I was on the phone with Grandma. She is okay. She is in a safe place. The storm will pass soon. Don't worry. Come inside with me. We can have some cookies and milk and read a story. How does that sound?"

Sara and Ben nod and smile. They are happy. They love Mom. They love Grandma. They love cookies and milk and stories. They are not scared anymore. They follow Mom into the house. The storm is still loud, but they don't mind. They are safe and warm and cozy. They are happy.

Sam and Mia are friends. They like to play with their toys in the park. One day, they find a big box. They open the box and see many shiny things inside. They see a cell, a watch, a necklace, and a ring.

"Wow, look at these!" Sam says. He picks up the cell and presses some buttons. "This is fun!"

"I want the cell too!" Mia says. She tries to grab the cell from Sam. "Give it to me!"

"No, it's mine!" Sam says. He holds the cell tight. "You can have the watch!"

"I don't want the watch, I want the cell!" Mia says. She pulls the cell hard. "Let go!"

They both pull the cell and fight. The cell breaks in half. They hear a loud beep. They see a red light on the cell.

"Oh no, what did we do?" Sam says. He drops the cell. "Is it broken?"

"I don't know, maybe it's a bomb!" Mia says. She runs away. "Help, help!"

A man comes to the park. He sees the box and the cell. He is angry. He is a spy. The cell is his. It is a dependable cell. He needs the cell to talk to his boss. He sees Sam and Mia.

"Hey, you kids, what did you do to my cell?" he says. He runs after them. "Give it back to me!"

Sam and Mia are scared. They run to their moms. They tell them what happened. Their moms hug them and take them home. They say they are sorry. They learn not to touch things that are not theirs. They hope the spy will not find them. They hope the cell will not explode.

Sam and Jen were best friends. They liked to play in the park with their toys. Sam had a red car that could zoom very fast. Jen had a pink bike that she could jog on. They had fun racing each other and making noises.

One day, they saw a big dog in the park. It was black and furry and had sharp teeth. It barked loud and ran after them. Sam and Jen were scared. They tried to get away, but the dog was faster. It caught up with Sam and bit his car. The car broke into pieces and stopped zooming. Sam cried and dropped his car. Jen stopped her bike and ran to him.

"Are you okay, Sam?" Jen asked. She hugged him and looked at his car. It was dead. It could not zoom anymore.

"I'm sorry, Jen. I should have listened to you. You told me not to zoom too close to the dog. But I wanted to win the race. I was silly and mean." Sam said. He felt bad and sorry.

"It's okay, Sam. I forgive you. You are my friend. But you have to be careful and kind. The dog was angry and scared. He did not like us zooming and jogging near him. He wanted to be left alone. We have to respect other animals and people." Jen said. She was wise and nice.

Sam and Jen learned a lesson. They said sorry to the dog and gave him a bone. The dog wagged his tail and licked their faces. He was happy and friendly. They played with him and their toys. They zoomed and jogged together, but not too fast or loud. They had fun and were safe.

Lily and Mom went to the mall. Lily liked the mall. She saw many toys and clothes and books. She wanted to touch everything. Mom said, "No, Lily, you have to stay with me. The mall is big and busy. You can get lost or hurt."

But Lily did not listen. She saw a gray cat in a pet shop. She loved cats. She ran to the cat and said, "Hello, kitty, you are so cute. Can I pet you?" She opened the cage and took the cat out. The cat was scared and angry. It scratched Lily's face and ran away.

Lily cried. She was in pain and she was sorry. She looked for Mom, but she could not see her. She saw many people and things, but not Mom. She felt alone and scared. She wanted Mom to protect her.

Mom heard Lily's cry. She was worried and angry. She ran to the pet shop and saw Lily's face. She said, "Lily, what did you do? You are hurt and you are naughty. You did not stay with me. You made the cat run away. You are in trouble."

She took Lily to the nurse. The nurse cleaned Lily's face and put a bandage on it. She said, "Lily, you have to be careful and listen to your mom. The cat was not your friend. It was wild and scared. You have to respect animals and their homes."

Lily was sad. She said, "I'm sorry, Mom. I'm sorry, nurse. I'm sorry, cat. I just wanted to play. I love you, Mom. Please don't be mad at me."

Mom hugged Lily. She said, "I love you, too, Lily. But you have to learn from your mistake. You have to obey me and stay with me. I want to protect you and keep you safe. Do you understand?"

Lily nodded. She said, "Yes, Mom. I understand. I will be good. Can we go home now?"

Mom said, "Yes, Lily. We can go home now. But you have to say sorry to the pet shop owner and pay for the cat's cage. And you have to be more careful next time."

Lily said, "OK, Mom. I will say sorry and pay. And I will be more careful. I don't want to get hurt or lose you again."

They left the mall. Lily was still sad and sore. She did not like the mall anymore. She learned a hard lesson. She wished she had listened to Mom. The end.

One day, Sam finds a big red fruit in the kitchen. He does not know what it is. He picks it up and feels it. It is round and smooth and heavy. He smells it. It has a sweet and sour smell. He wants to taste it.

He bites the fruit with his mouth. He feels a squirt of juice on his tongue. It is very sour and makes him pucker his mouth. He does not like it. He spits it out and makes a face. He says, "Yuck!"

Mom sees Sam and laughs. She says, "That is a lemon, Sam. It is not for eating by itself. It is for making lemonade or putting on fish. Do you want to try some lemonade?"

Sam nods. He likes lemonade. It is sweet and cold and refreshing. Mom cuts the lemon and squeezes it into a pitcher. She adds water and sugar and stirs it. She pours some lemonade into a cup and gives it to Sam.

Sam sips the lemonade with his mouth. He likes it. It is not too sour and not too sweet. It makes him smile. He says, "Yum!"

Mom smiles too. She says, "You are a good tester, Sam. You are brave and curious. But be careful, some things are not good for your mouth. Always ask me before you test something new, okay?"

Sam nods. He hugs Mom and says, "Okay, Mom. I love you. And I love lemonade."

Once upon a time, there was a little boy named Joe. He loved to play outside. One day, Joe saw a big blue top. He was so excited, he ran over to it. Joe picked up the top, put it on the ground, and started to spin it. He laughed as it spun round and round. 

The top stopped spinning, but Joe wanted it to keep going. He stepped away and yelled, "I want the top to spin!" 

Suddenly a voice came out of the sky. It said, "If Joe wants the top to keep spinning, he needs to take the spin test." 

Joe wasn't sure what a spin test was, but he was brave. He looked up and said, "Okay, I'll take the test!"

The voice said, "Good! To finish the spin test, you must spin the top until it stops by itself. Go ahead and try."

So Joe stepped forward, blew on the top to make it spin, and watched as it spun round and round. Finally, it stopped spinning on its own. Joe had passed the spin test! 

The voice said, "Congratulations Joe! Now the top will spin forever."

Joe was so happy, he jumped for joy! Now he could enjoy spinning his big blue top as long as he wanted.

As the spider worked on its new web, it saw a little bug walking towards it. The spider could tell the bug was weak and tired. The spider thought to itself, "I will catch this bug and help it get strong again."

The bug walked right into the spider's new web and got stuck. The spider crawled over to the bug and saw that it was nodding off to sleep. The spider carefully wrapped the bug up in its web and waited for it to wake up. When the bug woke up, it felt strong and healthy again. The spider was happy to have helped the little bug and went back to spinning beautiful cobwebs in its cozy corner of the big house.

"Ben, look what you did!" Lily cried. "You ruined my blanket! It has a hole in it! Give it back to me!"

Ben was shocked and scared. He did not mean to hurt the blanket. He did not know what to say. He let go of the blanket and ran away. He felt sorry and sad.

Lily hugged her blanket and sobbed. She wished she had not yelled at Ben. He was her friend and he did not deserve to be treated so badly. She realized that she had been selfish and mean. She wanted to say sorry to Ben and make up with him.

She got up and looked for Ben. She found him in his room, sitting on his bed. He looked lonely and hurt.

"Ben, I'm sorry," Lily said. "I was wrong to shout at you. You did not ruin my blanket. It was an accident. I should have been more careful and gentle with it. And I should have been more grateful and generous with you. You are more important than my blanket. Will you forgive me?"

Ben looked at Lily and saw that she was sincere and sorry. He felt a warm feeling in his heart. He nodded and smiled. He forgave Lily and hugged her.

They went back to the living room and mended the blanket together. They used some thread and a needle that their mom gave them. They made the hole smaller and stronger. They learned to be more careful and gentle with their things. And they learned to be more kind and loving with each other. They were happy and proud. They had a good lesson and a good day.

"Can we use the oats, Mom?" Tom asks.

"Yes, but be careful. Don't break the jar. It is glass and it can hurt you," Mom says.

Tom and Mia take the jar of oats and go to the table. They pour some oats in a bowl. They add milk and honey. They mix everything with a spoon.

"Look, we made oat dough!" Mia says.

"Let's make cookies!" Tom says.

They take some oat dough and roll it with their hands. They make round cookies and put them on a plate. They are happy.

But then, Tom sees a clear marble on the floor. He likes marbles. He wants to play with it.

"Look, a marble!" Tom says.

He runs to get the marble. He forgets about the jar of oats. He bumps into the jar. The jar falls from the table. It breaks into pieces. The oats spill everywhere.

"Oh no!" Mia says.

"Tom, what did you do?" Mom says.

Tom is scared. He sees the broken jar and the oats. He sees Mom's angry face. He feels bad.

"I'm sorry, Mom. I didn't mean to break the jar. I wanted the marble," Tom says.

Mom sighs. She is not happy, but she is not very mad. She knows Tom is young. She knows he made a mistake.

"It's okay, Tom. But you have to be more careful. Glass can cut you. And you wasted the oats. Now we can't make cookies," Mom says.

"I'm sorry, Mom. I'm sorry, Mia. Can we still be friends?" Tom says.

Mia looks at Tom. She is sad, but she is not very mad. She knows Tom is her friend. She knows he said sorry.

"Yes, Tom. We can still be friends. But next time, don't run in the kitchen. And don't touch the jar," Mia says.

Tom nods. He hugs Mia. He hugs Mom. He helps them clean the mess. He learns his lesson. He hopes to find more oats and make cookies another day.

Once upon a time, there were two friends, Hank and Sally. They loved to mix and play together. One day, they were playing together in the park and they spotted a big colorful box. Inside the box was a shiny big prize.

Hank and Sally both wanted the prize. They argued and argued, but neither of them would give it up. Suddenly, they heard a voice say, "The only way to decide who should get the prize is to take turns mixing up the box. Whoever is lucky and gets to the prize first can have it."

Hank and Sally took turns mixing up the box. When it was Sally's turn, the box suddenly opened and there was the big prize! She was so excited! She thanked her friend and quickly grabbed the prize.

Hank was disappointed, but he wasn't jealous. He was happy for Sally that she won the prize. He told her, "Lucky you, Sally!" Then he added, "It's better for friends to take turns sharing and caring than always trying to get the prize for themselves."

Sally and Hank hugged each other and from then on, they agreed that the prize would be shared equally. They were both happy, and the moral of the story is that sometimes it's better to share and care than to fight for a prize.

But then Bear said, "No, let's go now. We won't get this chance again."

So Rabbit and Bear rolled down the hill together. On the way down, Bear and Rabbit bumped into each other and spun around, laughing the whole way. They made it to the bottom of the hill, safe and sound.

The moral of the story is that we should take chances in life. Yet, before taking a chance, it's always best to think about safety first.

Lily didn't understand why she couldn't taste the bell and asked, "Why can't I taste it?"

Lily thought about it for a moment and decided that her mother was right. She decided to find something soft to taste instead. She touched a soft flower and smiled when she tasted the sweet scent.

Sara and Tom are twins. They like to play together in their room. They have many toys and books on the carpet. But sometimes they fight over the toys and books. They pull and push and yell at each other.

One day, Mom comes into their room. She sees the mess and the noise. She is not happy. She says, "Sara and Tom, you need to separate your toys and books. You can each have half of the carpet. Then you can play nicely and quietly."

Sara and Tom do not like this idea. They want to have all the toys and books. They say, "No, Mom, we don't want to separate. We want to share. We can play together."

Mom smiles. She says, "That's very good, Sara and Tom. Sharing is caring. But you also need to respect each other. You can't fight over the toys and books. You need to take turns and say please and thank you. Then you can have more fun and less trouble."

Sara and Tom agree. They say, "OK, Mom, we will try to respect each other. We will take turns and say please and thank you. We don't want to fight anymore. We want to be friends."

Mom hugs them. She says, "I'm proud of you, Sara and Tom. You are learning to be kind and polite. That's very important. Now you can play together on the carpet. But remember to clean up when you are done."

Sara and Tom nod. They say, "Yes, Mom, we will clean up. Thank you for helping us. We love you."

Mom leaves. Sara and Tom look at each other. They smile. They say, "We love you, too." They pick up a toy and a book. They start to play together on the carpet. They are happy.

The end.

Moral value: The story teaches the value of sharing, respecting, and being kind to others. It also shows the importance of listening to parents and cleaning up after playing.

"Wow, look at the cake!" Lily said. "Can we have some?"

"I don't know," Ben said. "Mom and Dad are still sleeping. Maybe we should wait."

But Lily was hungry and curious. She saw a knife on the counter. She took it and tried to cut a slice of cake.

"Be careful, Lily!" Ben said. "That knife is sharp. You could hurt yourself."

But Lily did not listen. She pushed the knife into the cake. But the knife slipped and cut her finger. She cried out loud.

Mom and Dad heard her cry and ran to the kitchen. They saw the blood and the cake. They were angry and worried.

"Lily, what did you do?" Mom said. "Why did you use the knife? You know it's dangerous."

"I'm sorry, Mom," Lily said. "I wanted some cake. It looked so yummy."

Mom and Dad hugged Lily and Ben. They cleaned Lily's finger and put a band-aid on it. They told them that they loved them, but they also scolded them for being naughty.

"You should never use a knife without our permission," Dad said. "And you should never eat cake before breakfast. It's not good for you."

Lily and Ben felt sorry and ashamed. They said they were sorry and they would not do it again.

Mom and Dad smiled and forgave them. They said they were grateful that Lily was not badly hurt. They said they made the cake for them to celebrate their birthday. They said they could have some cake later, after a healthy breakfast.

Lily and Ben thanked Mom and Dad. They hugged them and said they loved them. They learned their lesson. They learned to be patient, obedient, and grateful. They learned to be careful with knives. They learned to appreciate their parents' love. They learned to enjoy their birthday cake.
